# Investigation: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes in Terraform

**Repository:** hashicorp/terraform
**Task Type:** Deep Causal Chain (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

A Terraform user reports that `terraform plan` consistently shows resources "will be updated in-place" even though **no configuration changes** have been made. The phantom update appears for any resource that has provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes (e.g., `password`, `secret_key`).

The user is managing a VPN tunnel resource:

```hcl
resource "test_instance" "example" {
  ami      = "ami-12345"
  password = var.db_password  # provider schema marks 'password' as Sensitive: true
}
```

After a successful `terraform apply`, immediately running `terraform plan` shows:

```
  # test_instance.example will be updated in-place
  ~ resource "test_instance" "example" {
        id       = "i-abc123"
        # (1 unchanged attribute hidden)
    }

Plan: 0 to add, 1 to change, 0 to destroy.
```

There are **no actual attribute changes** — the before and after values are identical. The phantom diff occurs specifically for resources where the provider schema declares one or more attributes with `Sensitive: true`.

Additionally, `terraform show -json` on the state file shows that the `sensitive_values` section in the JSON output is **incomplete** — it lists sensitivity marks that came from variable references (e.g., `var.db_password` is a `sensitive` variable) but **omits** sensitivity marks from the provider schema itself (e.g., the `password` attribute is always sensitive regardless of how it's populated).

Running `terraform plan -refresh-only` also shows phantom changes, and `terraform import` followed by `terraform plan` shows even more phantom updates.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause of why Terraform generates phantom in-place updates for resources with schema-sensitive attributes, and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:

1. **How provider responses flow through the graph evaluator** — when `ReadResource` (refresh) or `PlanResourceChange` (plan) returns a value from the provider, how does `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` process that response? Specifically, examine `readResourceInstanceState()` (refresh path) and `plan()` (plan path) in `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`.

2. **The sensitivity mark gap** — the provider response comes back **without** any sensitivity marks (providers don't mark values; that's Terraform's responsibility). The code re-applies marks from the **prior state** (`priorPaths` from `AttrSensitivePaths`), but these only contain marks from sensitive variable references, NOT from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations.

3. **How state serialization records incomplete sensitivity** — when the instance object is written to state via `internal/states/instance_object.go`, `sensitive_attributes` in the state file only has paths from sensitive references, missing the schema-defined sensitive paths. Trace through how `AttrSensitivePaths` is populated and how `unmarkValueForStorage` extracts marks before state serialization.

4. **The evaluator's compensating workaround** — `internal/terraform/evaluate.go`'s `GetResource()` method was the ONLY place that applied schema marks (via `markProviderSensitiveAttributes()` or similar). This meant that when a value was read FROM state and decoded for expression evaluation, it would get schema marks added. But the value stored IN state never had those marks. This created an asymmetry.

5. **How the asymmetry produces phantom diffs** — the plan compares refreshed state (which has schema marks from the evaluator) against the planned state (which was built from provider response without schema marks). The mark difference causes the plan to detect a "change" even though the underlying values are identical. The diff is in the sensitivity metadata, not the attribute values themselves.

6. **The JSON output manifestation** — `internal/command/` layer functions that produce `terraform show -json` read `sensitive_attributes` from state, which is incomplete. This produces incorrect `sensitive_values` in JSON plan/state output, where schema-defined sensitive attributes are missing from the sensitivity map.

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Causal Chain
<Ordered list: symptom → intermediate hops → root cause>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- The causal chain spans at least 4 packages: `internal/terraform/` (graph evaluation + marks), `internal/states/` (state serialization), `internal/command/` (JSON output), and the provider interaction boundary
- Focus on how `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` handles provider responses, how `marks.go` applies sensitivity, how `instance_object.go` serializes state, and how `evaluate.go` compensates

// NodeAbstractResourceInstance represents a resource instance with no
// associated operations. It embeds NodeAbstractResource but additionally
// contains an instance key, used to identify one of potentially many
// instances that were created from a resource in configuration, e.g. using
// the "count" or "for_each" arguments.
type NodeAbstractResourceInstance struct {
	NodeAbstractResource
	Addr addrs.AbsResourceInstance

	// These are set via the AttachState method.
	instanceState *states.ResourceInstance

	Dependencies []addrs.ConfigResource

	preDestroyRefresh bool

	// During import we may generate configuration for a resource, which needs
	// to be stored in the final change.
	generatedConfigHCL string

	// override is set by the graph itself, just before this node executes.
	override *configs.Override
}

// NewNodeAbstractResourceInstance creates an abstract resource instance graph
// node for the given absolute resource instance address

    16→// object associated with a resource instance. In practice not all remote
    17→// objects are actually remote in the sense of being accessed over the network,
    18→// but this is the most common case.
    19→//
    20→// It is not valid to mutate a ResourceInstanceObject once it has been created.
    21→// Instead, create a new object and replace the existing one.

    24→	// Terraform.

    26→
    27→	// Private is an opaque value set by the provider when this object was
    28→	// last created or updated. Terraform Core does not use this value in
    29→	// any way and it is not exposed anywhere in the user interface, so
    30→	// a provider can use it for retaining any necessary private state.
    31→	Private []byte
    32→
    33→	// Status represents the "readiness" of the object as of the last time
    34→	// it was updated.
    35→	Status ObjectStatus
    36→
    37→	// Dependencies is a set of absolute address to other resources this
    38→	// instance dependeded on when it was applied. This is used to construct
    39→	// the dependency relationships for an object whose configuration is no
    40→	// longer available, such as if it has been removed from configuration
    41→	// altogether, or i

    13→
    14→// ResourceInstanceObjectSrc is a not-fully-decoded version of
    15→// ResourceInstanceObject. Decoding of it can be completed by first handling
    16→// any schema migration steps to get to the latest schema version and then
    17→// calling method Decode with the implied type of the latest schema.
    18→type ResourceInstanceObjectSrc struct {
    19→	// SchemaVersion is the resource-type-specific schema version number that
    20→	// was current when either AttrsJSON or AttrsFlat was encoded. Migration
    21→	// steps are required if this is less than the current version number
    22→	// reported by the corresponding provider.
    23→	SchemaVersion uint64
    24→

    13→// copyAndExtendPath returns a copy of a cty.Path with some additional
    14→// `cty.PathStep`s appended to its end, to simplify creating new child paths.
    15→func copyAndExtendPath(path cty.Path, nextSteps ...cty.PathStep) cty.Path {
    16→	newPath := make(cty.Path, len(path), len(path)+len(nextSteps))
    17→	copy(newPath, path)
    18→	newPath = append(newPath, nextSteps...)
    19→	return newPath
    20→}
    21→
    22→// ValueMarks returns a set of path value marks for a given value and path,
    23→// based on the sensitive flag for each attribute within the schema. Nested
    24→// blocks are descended (if present in the given value).
    25→func (b *Block) ValueMarks(val cty.Value, path cty.Path) []cty.PathValueMarks {
    26→	var pvm []cty.PathValueMarks
    27→
    28→	// We can mark attributes as sensitive even if the value is null
    29→	for name, attrS := range b.Attributes {
    30→		if attrS.Sensitive {
    31→			// Create a copy of the path, with this step added, to add to our PathValueMarks slice
    32→			attrPath := copyAndExtendPath(path, cty.GetAttrStep{Name: name})
    33→			pvm = append(pvm, cty.PathValueMarks{
    34→				Path:  attrPath,
    35→				Marks: cty.NewValueMarks(marks.Sensitive),
    36→			})
    37→		}
    38→	}
    39→
    40→	// If the value is null, no other marks are possible
    41→	if val.IsNull() {
    42→		return pvm
    43→	}
    44→
    45→	// Extract marks for nested attribute type values
    46→	for name, attrS := range b.Attribut
... (truncated)

    40→//
    41→// Blocks themselves cannot be sensitive as a whole -- sensitivity is a
    42→// per-attribute idea -- but sometimes we want to include a whole object
    43→// decoded from a block in some UI output, and that is safe to do only if
    44→// none of the contained attributes are sensitive.
    45→func (b *Block) ContainsSensitive() bool {
    46→	for _, attrS := range b.Attributes {
    47→		if attrS.Sensitive {
    48→			return true
    49→		}
    50→		if attrS.NestedType != nil && attrS.NestedType.ContainsSensitive() {
    51→			return true
    52→		}
    53→	}
    54→	for _, blockS := range b.BlockTypes {
    55→		if blockS.ContainsSensitive() {
    56→			return true
    57→		}
    58→	}
    59→	return false
    60→}
    61→
    62→// ImpliedType returns the cty.Type that would result from decoding a Block's
    63→// ImpliedType and getting the resulting AttributeType.
    64→//
    65→// ImpliedType always returns a result, even if the given schema is
    66→// inconsistent. Code that creates configschema.Object objects should be tested
    67→// using the InternalValidate method to detect any inconsistencies that would
    68→// cause this method to fall back on defaults and assumptions.
    69→func (a *Attribute) ImpliedType() cty.Type {
    70→	if a.NestedType != nil {
    71→		return a.NestedType.specType().WithoutOptionalAttributesDeep()
    72→	}
    73→	return a.Type
    74→}

    13→// filterMarks removes any PathValueMarks from marks which cannot be applied to
    14→// the given value. When comparing existing marks to those from a map or other
    15→// dynamic value, we may not have values at the same paths and need to strip
    16→// out irrelevant marks.
    17→func filterMarks(val cty.Value, marks []cty.PathValueMarks) []cty.PathValueMarks {
    18→	var res []cty.PathValueMarks
    19→	for _, mark := range marks {
    20→		// any error here just means the path cannot apply to this value, so we
    21→		// don't need this mark for comparison.
    22→		if _, err := mark.Path.Apply(val); err == nil {
    23→			res = append(res, mark)
    24→		}
    25→	}
    26→	return res
    27→}
    28→
    29→// marksEqual compares 2 unordered sets of PathValue marks for equality, with
    30→// the comparison using the cty.PathValueMarks.Equal method.
    31→func marksEqual(a, b []cty.PathValueMarks) bool {
    32→	if len(a) == 0 && len(b) == 0 {
    33→		return true
    34→	}
    35→
    36→	if len(a) != len(b) {
    37→		return false
    38→	}
    39→
    40→	less := func(s []cty.PathValueMarks) func(i, j int) bool {
    41→		return func(i, j int) bool {
    42→			// the sort only needs to be consistent, so use the GoString format
    43→			// to get a comparable value
    44→			return fmt.Sprintf("%#v", s[i]) < fmt.Sprintf("%#v", s[j])
    45→		}
    46→	}

    48→	sort.Slice(a, less(a))
    49→	sort.Slice(b, less(b))

## Comprehensive Report: Sensitivity Marks and Sensitive Attributes in Terraform

### 1. **Core Sensitivity Mark Handling Files**

#### `/workspace/internal/terraform/marks.go`
Contains two utility functions for handling sensitivity marks:

**Line 17-27: `filterMarks(val cty.Value, marks []cty.PathValueMarks) []cty.PathValueMarks`**
- Removes any PathValueMarks that cannot be applied to the given value
- Used when comparing marks from dynamic values that may differ in structure
- Iterates through marks and validates each path can be applied to the value

**Line 31-58: `marksEqual(a, b []cty.PathValueMarks) bool`**
- Compares two unordered sets of PathValueMarks for equality
- Sorts both slices to ensure consistent comparison
- Returns true only if both slices contain identical marks in the same order after sorting

- Examines nested types within attributes

    77→func (os *ResourceInstanceObjectSrc) Decode(ty cty.Type) (*ResourceInstanceObject, error) {
    78→	var val cty.Value
    79→	var err error
    80→	if os.AttrsFlat != nil {
    81→		// Legacy mode. We'll do our best to unpick this from the flatmap.
    82→		val, err = hcl2shim.HCL2ValueFromFlatmap(os.AttrsFlat, ty)
    83→		if err != nil {
    84→			return nil, err
    85→		}
    86→	} else {
    87→		val, err = ctyjson.Unmarshal(os.AttrsJSON, ty)
    88→		// Mark the value with paths if applicable
    89→		if os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {
    90→			val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)
    91→		}
    92→		if err != nil {
    93→			return nil, err
    94→		}
    95→	}
    96→
    97→	return &ResourceInstanceObject{

    13→// filterMarks removes any PathValueMarks from marks which cannot be applied to
    14→// the given value. When comparing existing marks to those from a map or other
    15→// dynamic value, we may not have values at the same paths and need to strip
    16→// out irrelevant marks.
    17→func filterMarks(val cty.Value, marks []cty.PathValueMarks) []cty.PathValueMarks {
    18→	var res []cty.PathValueMarks
    19→	for _, mark := range marks {
    20→		// any error here just means the path cannot apply to this value, so we
    21→		// don't need this mark for comparison.
    22→		if _, err := mark.Path.Apply(val); err == nil {
    23→			res = append(res, mark)
    24→		}
    25→	}
    26→	return res
    27→}

    44→			return fmt.Sprintf("%#v", s[i]) < fmt.Sprintf("%#v", s[j])
    45→		}
    46→	}

Perfect! Now I have the full picture. Let me compile a comprehensive report with all the findings:

## Investigation Report: Phantom Update Asymmetry in Terraform

Based on my thorough investigation of the codebase, I've identified a critical asymmetry that causes phantom updates. Here are the specific findings:

---

## 1. REFRESH() METHOD - Marks Handling

**File:** `/workspace/internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`  
**Lines:** 580-723

### Refresh marks removal and re-application:

```go
// Line 622-626: Unmark before sending to provider
var priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks
if priorVal.ContainsMarked() {
    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()
}

// Line 684: Normalize refreshed state from provider
newState := objchange.NormalizeObjectFromLegacySDK(resp.NewState, schema)

// Line 717-720: RE-APPLY MARKS AFTER REFRESH
ret := state.DeepCopy()
ret.Value = newState
ret.Private = resp.Private

// ...

// CRITICAL ASYMMETRY: Only prior marks are re-applied
if len(priorPaths) > 0 {
    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)
}
```

**Key Issue:** The refresh method:
- Extracts marks from the PRIOR state before sending to provider
- Receives unmarked state back from provider
- Re-applies ONLY the marks from priorPaths (sensitivity marks from state file)
- **Does NOT apply schema-derived marks** (which would be `schema.ValueMarks()`)

---

**Lines:** 725-1210

   168→// marshalPlanResources
   169→func marshalPlanResources(changes *plans.Changes, ris []addrs.AbsResourceInstance, schemas *terraform.Schemas) ([]resource, error) {
   170→	var ret []resource
   171→
   172→	for _, ri := range ris {
   173→		r := changes.ResourceInstance(ri)
   174→		if r.Action == plans.Delete {
   175→			continue
   176→		}
   177→
   178→		resource := resource{
   179→			Address:      r.Addr.String(),
   180→			Type:         r.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,
   181→			Name:         r.Addr.Resource.Resource.Name,
   182→			ProviderName: r.ProviderAddr.Provider.String(),
   183→			Index:        r.Addr.Resource.Key,
   184→		}
   185→
   186→		switch r.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode {
   187→		case addrs.ManagedResourceMode:
   188→			resource.Mode = "managed"
   189→		case addrs.DataResourceMode:
   190→			resource.Mode = "data"
   191→		default:
   192→			return nil, fmt.Errorf("resource %s has an unsupported mode %s",
   193→				r.Addr.String(),
   194→				r.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode.String(),
   195→			)
   196→		}
   197→
   198→		schema, schemaVer := schemas.ResourceTypeConfig(
   199→			r.ProviderAddr.Provider,
   200→			r.Addr.Resource.Resource.Mode,
   201→			resource.Type,

263-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed the investigation and written a comprehensive report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. 

## Summary

I've successfully traced the phantom in-place update issue through the Terraform codebase and identified the root cause: **a critical asymmetry in sensitivity mark propagation**.

### Key Findings:

1. **The Asymmetry**: Schema-derived sensitivity marks are applied ONLY during expression evaluation (in `evaluate.go` lines 714-723), but NOT during:
   - State encoding (stored to file without schema marks)
   - State decoding (restored without schema marks)
   - Refresh execution (doesn't re-apply schema marks)
   - Plan comparison (uses incomplete mark set)

2. **The Phantom Update Trigger** (line 1208 of `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`):
   ```go
   if action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {
       action = plans.Update  // Incorrectly changed!
   }
   ```
   This compares config marks vs refreshed-state marks, but the refreshed state never had schema marks applied, causing a "change" detection in metadata even when values are identical.

3. **The Causal Chain**:
   - State is stored WITHOUT schema marks (by design—they're transient)
   - State is decoded WITHOUT schema marks
   - Refresh re-applies only reference marks, not schema marks
   - Plan compares incomplete mark sets
   - Schema marks are finally applied too late (during evaluation, after planning)
   - Result: Phantom Update action for resources with schema-sensitive attributes

4. **Affected Span**: 4+ packages (`internal/terraform`, `internal/states`, `internal/command`) with the core issue in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go:718-720` (refresh) and line 1208 (plan comparison).

The report includes specific file paths, line

Since it cannot be moved into the\n    64\u2192\t// ObjectRead state, a tainted object must be replaced.\n    65\u2192\tObjectTainted ObjectStatus = 'T'\n    66\u2192\n    67\u2192\t// ObjectPlanned is a special object status used only for the transient\n    68\u2192\t// placeholder objects we place into state during the refresh and plan\n    69\u2192\t// walks to stand in for objects that will be created during apply.\n    70\u2192\t//\n    71\u2192\t// Any object of this status must have a corresponding change recorded\n    72\u2192\t// in the current plan, whose value must then be used in preference to\n    73\u2192\t// the value stored in state when evaluating expressions. A planned\n    74\u2192\t// object stored in state will be incomplete if any of its attributes are\n    75\u2192\t// not yet known, and the plan must be consulted in order to \"see\" those\n    76\u2192\t// unknown values, because the state is not able to represent them.\n    77\u2192\tObjectPlanned ObjectStatus = 'P'\n    78\u2192)\n    79\u2192\n    80\u2192// Encode marshals the value within the receiver to produce a\n    81\u2192// ResourceInstanceObjectSrc ready to be written to a state file.\n    82\u2192//\n    83\u2192// The given type must be the implied type of the resource type schema, and\n    84\u2192// the given value must conform to it. It is important to pass the schema\n    85\u2192// type and not the object's own type so that dynamically-typed attributes\n    86\u2192// will be stored correctly. The caller must also provide the version number\n    87\u2192// of the schema that the given type was derived from, which will be recorded\n    88\u2192// in the source object so it can be used to detect when schema migration is\n    89\u2192// required on read.\n    90\u2192//\n    91\u2192// The returned object may share internal references with the receiver and\n    92\u2192// so the caller must not mutate the receiver any further once once this\n    93\u2192// method is called.\n    94\u2192func (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\n    95\u2192\t// If it contains marks, remove these marks before traversing the\n    96\u2192\t// structure with UnknownAsNull, and save the PathValueMarks\n    97\u2192\t// so we can save them in state.\n    98\u2192\tval, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    99\u2192\n   100\u2192\t// Our state serialization can't represent unknown values, so we convert\n   101\u2192\t// them to nulls here. The apply step should never produce unknown\n   107\u2192\t// values, but if it does it's the responsibility of the caller to detect\n   108\u2192\t// and raise an error about that.\n   109\u2192\tval = cty.UnknownAsNull(val)\n   110\u2192\n   111\u2192\tsrc, err := ctyjson.Marshal(val, ty)\n   112\u2192\tif err != nil {\n   113\u2192\t\treturn nil, err\n   114\u2192\t}\n   115\u2192\n   116\u2192\t// Dependencies are collected and merged in an unordered format (using map\n   117\u2192\t// keys as a set), then later changed to a slice (in random ordering) to be\n   118\u2192\t// stored in state as an array. To avoid pointless thrashing of state in\n   119\u2192\t// refresh-only runs, we can either override comparison of dependency lists\n   120\u2192\t// (more desirable, but tricky for Reasons) or just sort when encoding.\n   121\u2192\t// Encoding of instances can happen concurrently, so we must copy the\n   122\u2192\t// dependencies to avoid mutating what may be a shared array of values.\n   123\u2192\tdependencies := make([]addrs.ConfigResource, len(o.Dependencies))\n   124\u2192\tcopy(dependencies, o.Dependencies)\n   125\u2192\n   126\u2192\tsort.Slice(dependencies, func(i, j int) bool { return dependencies[i].String() < dependencies[j].String() })\n   127\u2192\n   128\u2192\treturn &ResourceInstanceObjectSrc{\n   129\u2192\t\tSchemaVersion:       schemaVersion,\n   130\u2192\t\tAttrsJSON:           src,\n   131\u2192\t\tAttrSensitivePaths:  pvm,\n   132\u2192\t\tPrivate:             o.Private,\n   133\u2192\t\tStatus:              o.Status,\n   134\u2192\t\tDependencies:        dependencies,\n   135\u2192\t\tCreateBeforeDestroy: o.CreateBeforeDestroy,\n   136\u2192\t}, nil\n   137\u2192}\n   138\u2192\n   139\u2192// AsTainted returns a deep copy of the receiver with the status updated to\n   140\u2192// ObjectTainted.\n   141\u2192func (o *ResourceInstanceObject) AsTainted() *ResourceInstanceObject {\n   142\u2192\tif o == nil {\n   143\u2192\t\t// A nil object can't be tainted, but we'll allow this anyway to\n   144\u2192\t\t// avoid a crash, since we presumably intend to eventually record\n   145\u2192\t\t// the object has having been deleted anyway.\n   146\u2192\t\treturn nil\n   147\u2192\t}\n   148\u2192\tret := o.DeepCopy()\n   149\u2192\tret.Status = ObjectTainted\n   150\u2192\treturn ret\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.   "content": "# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes in Terraform\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform generates phantom in-place update actions for resources with schema-defined sensitive attributes due to an asymmetry in how sensitivity marks are handled: schema-derived sensitivity marks are applied only during expression evaluation (in `evaluate.go`), not during the refresh-to-plan comparison phase in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`. This causes the mark-based action override at line 1208 to incorrectly convert NoOp to Update when schema-sensitive attributes are present, even though the underlying attribute values are identical.\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a critical asymmetry in sensitivity mark propagation across three phases:\n\n1. **Refresh Phase** (`node_resource_abstract_instance.go:718-720`): Marks from prior state are extracted, provider is called with unmarked values, and then only the extracted marks are re-applied. Schema-derived marks are NOT applied.\n\n2. **Plan Comparison Phase** (`node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208`): A mark-equality check compares config marks against refresh marks. Because schema marks were never applied to the refreshed state, the mark sets differ, triggering an erroneous action upgrade from NoOp to Update.\n\n3. **Expression Evaluation Phase** (`evaluate.go:714-723`): Schema-derived marks ARE applied when values are read for expression evaluation, but this happens AFTER planning and is NOT reflected in the plan comparison.\n\nThis creates a cascade where:\n- State is stored WITHOUT schema marks (line `instance_object.go:131`)\n- State is decoded without schema marks (line `instance_object_src.go:90`)\n- Refresh doesn't apply schema marks (line `node_resource_abstract_instance.go:718-720`)\n- Plan comparison uses incomplete mark information (line `node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208`)\n- Schema marks are only applied later during evaluation (line `evaluate.go:718-723`)\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. Refresh Does Not Apply Schema Marks\n\n**File**: `/workspace/internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`\n**Lines**: 620-720\n\n```go\n// Line 620: Load state value (only has reference marks from decode)\npriorVal := state.Value\n\n// Lines 624-626: Extract only reference marks\nvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\nif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()  // priorPaths = reference marks only\n}\n\n// Lines 636-641: Send unmarked to provider\nresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n    TypeName:     n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n    PriorState:   priorVal,  // UNMARKED\n    ...\n})\n\n// Line 684: Receive unmarked response\nnewState := objchange.NormalizeObjectFromLegacySDK(resp.NewState, schema)\n\n// Lines 717-720: RE-APPLY ONLY REFERENCE MARKS (NOT SCHEMA MARKS)\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)  // Only reference marks!\n}\n// Missing: schema marks are NOT applied here\n```\n\n**Critical Gap**: The refresh method has access to `schema` (line 598) but never calls `schema.ValueMarks()` to apply schema-derived sensitivity marks.\n\n### 2. State Storage Only Preserves Reference Marks\n\n**File**: `/workspace/internal/states/instance_object.go`\n**Lines**: 94-137\n\n```go\nfunc (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\n    // Line 98: Unmark the value to enable JSON serialization\n    val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()  // pvm = all marks from value\n\n    // Lines 128-136: Store only what was marked in the value\n    return &ResourceInstanceObjectSrc{\n        SchemaVersion:      schemaVersion,\n        AttrsJSON:          src,\n        AttrSensitivePaths: pvm,  // Stores ONLY marks that were on the value\n        Private:            o.Private,\n        ...\n    }, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Why This Matters**: The state file stores `AttrSensitivePaths`, which only contains marks that were physically on the cty.Value object. Schema-derived marks are NOT stored because they're applied at evaluation time, not at state serialization time. This is by design\u2014marks should not be double-stored. But it creates a gap when comparing during planning.\n\n### 3. State Decoding Restores Only Reference Marks\n\n**File**: `/workspace/internal/states/instance_object_src.go`\n**Lines**: 77-104\n\n```go\nfunc (os *ResourceInstanceObjectSrc) Decode(ty cty.Type) (*ResourceInstanceObject, error) {\n    // Line 87: Unmarshal from JSON\n    val, err = ctyjson.Unmarshal(os.AttrsJSON, ty)\n\n    // Lines 89-91: Re-apply ONLY stored reference marks\n    if os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n        val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)  // Only reference marks\n    }\n    // Missing: schema marks NOT applied here\n\n    return &ResourceInstanceObject{\n        Value: val,  // Has reference marks only\n        ...\n    }, nil\n}\n```\n\n### 4. The Plan Comparison Asymmetry\n\n**File**: `/workspace/internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`\n**Lines**: 868-1208\n\n**Step 1: Extract marks from inputs (lines 868-869)**\n```go\nunmarkedConfigVal, unmarkedPaths := configValIgnored.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()  // Config marks\nunmarkedPriorVal, priorPaths := priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()             // Reference marks only!\n```\n\n**Step 2: Call provider with unmarked values (lines 902-909)**\n```go\nresp = provider.PlanResourceChange(providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest{\n    TypeName:         n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n    Config:           unmarkedConfigVal,\n    PriorState:       unmarkedPriorVal,    // UNMARKED (no schema marks)\n    ProposedNewState: proposedNewVal,\n    PriorPrivate:     priorPrivate,\n    ProviderMeta:     metaConfigVal,\n})\n```\n\n**Step 3: Provider returns unmarked planned state (lines 916-1000)**\n```go\nplannedNewVal := resp.PlannedState\n...\n// Re-apply config marks to planned value\nif len(unmarkedPaths) > 0 {\n    plannedNewVal = plannedNewVal.MarkWithPaths(unmarkedPaths)  // Apply config marks\n}\n```\n\n**Step 4: THE PHANTOM UPDATE TRIGGER (lines 1208-1210)**\n```go\n// line 1082-1083: Basic value equality check (unmarked comparison)\neqV := unmarkedPlannedNewVal.Equals(unmarkedPriorVal)\neq := eqV.IsKnown() && eqV.True()\n\n// lines 1085-1091: If values are equal, set action to NoOp\nvar action plans.Action\nswitch {\ncase priorVal.IsNull():\n    action = plans.Create\ncase eq && !matchedForceReplace:\n    action = plans.NoOp  // <- Values are equal\n\n// LINE 1208: THIS CONVERTS NoOp TO Update BASED ON MARK DIFFERENCES\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update  // <- PHANTOM UPDATE!\n}\n```\n\n**The Comparison Being Made**:\n- **Planned value marks**: `filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths)` = config marks from configuration\n- **Prior value marks**: `priorPaths` = reference marks from refreshed state (NO schema marks!)\n\n**Why This Causes Phantom Updates**:\n\nWhen a provider schema declares an attribute as sensitive:\n\n| Phase | What Happens | Marks Present |\n|-------|-------------|---------------|\n| Encode to state file | Unmark value before JSON serialization | Reference marks only (if any) |\n| Decode from state file | Restore reference marks only | Reference marks only |\n| Refresh execute | Re-apply reference marks, NOT schema marks | Reference marks only |\n| Plan extract prior marks | Extract marks from refreshed state | Reference marks only |\n| Plan extract config marks | Extract marks from config | Config marks (possibly different!) |\n| **Plan comparison at line 1208** | **Compare: config marks vs reference marks** | **DIFFERENT!** |\n| Result | Action changed from NoOp to Update | **Phantom Update!** |\n\n### 5. Schema Marks Are Applied ONLY During Expression Evaluation\n\n**File**: `/workspace/internal/terraform/evaluate.go`\n**Lines**: 714-723\n\n```go\n// Decode state value (has reference marks only from state file)\nios, err := is.Current.Decode(ty)\n...\nval := ios.Value  // Has reference marks only\n\n// THIS IS WHERE SCHEMA MARKS ARE APPLIED, BUT ONLY FOR EVALUATION\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()  // Remove reference marks\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)  // ADD schema marks\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)  // Re-apply combined marks\n}\ninstances[key] = val  // Value now has schema marks for expression evaluation\n```\n\n**Critical Point**: Schema marks are applied here (line 718-723), but this is AFTER planning. The marks applied here are NOT reflected in the plan file or the plan comparison.\n\nAdditionally, at lines 689-695, for planned changes:\n```go\nafterMarks := change.AfterValMarks\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    afterMarks = append(afterMarks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)  // Schema marks added\n}\ninstances[key] = val.MarkWithPaths(afterMarks)\n```\n\nThis applies schema marks for expression evaluation, but these marks are NOT stored in the plan file or used in the plan comparison logic.\n\n### 6. Marks Utility Functions\n\n**File**: `/workspace/internal/terraform/marks.go`\n**Lines**: 17-58\n\n```go\n// Line 31-58: marksEqual compares two sets of marks\nfunc marksEqual(a, b []cty.PathValueMarks) bool {\n    // Unordered comparison of path/mark sets\n    ...\n}\n\n// Line 17-27: filterMarks removes marks that don't apply to a value\nfunc filterMarks(val cty.Value, marks []cty.PathValueMarks) []cty.PathValueMarks {\n    // Returns only marks that can be applied to val\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nThese functions are used at line 1208 to compare mark sets, but they operate on incomplete mark information (missing schema marks).\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`** (1270 lines)\n   - `refresh()` method (lines 580-723): Doesn't apply schema marks after refresh\n   - `plan()` method (lines 725-1268): Mark comparison logic at line 1208\n\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`** (150 lines)\n   - `Encode()` method (lines 94-137): Stores only reference marks\n\n3. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`** (150+ lines)\n   - `Decode()` method (lines 77-104): Restores only reference marks\n\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** (800+ lines)\n   - `GetResource()` method (lines 680-725): Applies schema marks for evaluation only\n\n5. **`internal/terraform/marks.go`** (60 lines)\n   - `marksEqual()` and `filterMarks()` functions: Compare incomplete mark sets\n\n6. **`internal/command/jsonplan/values.go`** (250 lines)\n   - `marshalPlanResources()` (lines 169-245): Uses marks from plan (which lack schema marks)\n\n7. **`internal/command/jsonstate/state.go`** (500 lines)\n   - `State()` method (lines 400-411, 453-462): Correctly applies schema marks when generating JSON output (but plan generation doesn't)\n\n8. **Provider RPC boundary**:\n   - Provider receives unmarked values\n   - Provider returns unmarked values\n   - All sensitivity marking is Terraform's responsibility\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Initial Symptom**: User reports phantom in-place updates after `terraform apply` with no config changes\n\n2. **Intermediate Hop 1 - State Storage**: When state is encoded for storage (lines 94-137 in `instance_object.go`), schema-derived marks are NOT stored because they are considered transient marks applied only at evaluation time. State stores only reference marks (marks from sensitive variable references).\n\n3. **Intermediate Hop 2 - State Decoding**: When state is decoded for use in subsequent operations (lines 77-104 in `instance_object_src.go`), only the stored reference marks are restored. Schema marks are missing.\n\n4. **Intermediate Hop 3 - Refresh Execution**: During `terraform refresh` (lines 580-723 in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`), the code:\n   - Extracts marks from the prior state (only reference marks)\n   - Sends unmarked value to provider\n   - Receives unmarked response\n   - Re-applies only the extracted reference marks (line 718-720)\n   - Does NOT apply schema marks (never calls `schema.ValueMarks()`)\n\n5. **Intermediate Hop 4 - Plan Starts**: In the plan phase (lines 725+), the code receives the refreshed state as \"prior state.\" This prior state has only reference marks, NOT schema marks.\n\n6. **Intermediate Hop 5 - Mark Extraction**: Config marks are extracted from configuration (line 868), prior marks are extracted from refreshed state (line 869). These may differ:\n   - Config marks depend on what variables are used (e.g., is `password = var.db_password`?)\n   - Prior marks depend on what was stored in state (only reference marks)\n   - Schema marks are NOT in either set\n\n7. **ROOT CAUSE - Phantom Update Trigger** (line 1208): The plan comparison logic checks if marks are equal. Because schema marks were never applied to the refreshed state, the mark comparison fails even though the values are identical:\n   ```go\n   if action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n       action = plans.Update  // <- WRONG!\n   }\n   ```\n   - `filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths)`: config marks from config\n   - `priorPaths`: reference marks from state (missing schema marks!)\n   - These are different \u2192 action changed to Update\n\n8. **Final Symptom**: Plan shows resource \"will be updated in-place\" even though no actual attribute values changed, only sensitivity mark metadata differs.\n\n## Recommendation\n\nThe fix requires applying schema-derived sensitivity marks at the appropriate point in the refresh\u2192plan flow:\n\n**Option A (Recommended)**: Apply schema marks during refresh after receiving the provider response.\n\nIn `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, modify the `refresh()` method (around lines 717-720) to:\n```go\n// Mark the value if necessary\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}\n\n// ADDITION: Also apply schema-derived marks\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    unmarked, marks := ret.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(unmarked, nil)...)\n    ret.Value = unmarked.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\n```\n\nThis ensures the refreshed state has both reference marks AND schema marks before being passed to the plan phase.\n\n**Option B**: Apply schema marks when extracting prior marks in the plan phase.\n\nIn `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, modify the `plan()` method (around lines 868-869) to ensure schema marks are included when extracting `priorPaths`.\n\n**Option C**: Store schema marks in state files.\n\nModify `instance_object.go` to calculate and store schema-derived marks in `AttrSensitivePaths`, though this requires schema context during state serialization.\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Enable trace-level logging for mark operations and compare marks applied at refresh vs marks used in plan comparison\n2. Verify that schema marks are missing from refreshed state when compared to the planned value's marks\n3. Confirm that phantom updates disappear once schema marks are applied during refresh\n4. Check that `terraform show -json` on state and plan JSON outputs correctly show `sensitive_values` for schema-defined sensitive attributes (this is already handled correctly in `jsonstate.go` but may be missing from `jsonplan.go`)\n\n## Key Files Summary\n\n| File | Lines | Function | Issue |\n|------|-------|----------|-------|\n| `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` | 718-720 | `refresh()` | Doesn't apply schema marks |\n| `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` | 868-869 | `plan()` | Extracts incomplete mark set (no schema marks) |\n| `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` | 1208 | `plan()` | Compares incomplete marks, triggers phantom update |\n| `instance_object.go` | 94-137 | `Encode()` | Stores only reference marks |\n| `instance_object_src.go` | 77-104 | `Decode()` | Restores only reference marks |\n| `evaluate.go` | 714-723 | `GetResource()` | Applies schema marks too late (after planning) |\n| `marks.go` | 31-58 | `marksEqual()` | Called with incomplete mark sets |\n| `jsonplan/values.go` | 212-235 | `marshalPlanResources()` | Plan JSON may lack schema marks |\n",

State Storage**: When state is encoded for storage (lines 94-137 in `instance_object.go`), schema-derived marks are NOT stored because they are considered transient marks applied only at evaluation time. State stores only reference marks (marks from sensitive variable references).\n\n3. **Intermediate Hop 2 - State Decoding**: When state is decoded for use in subsequent operations (lines 77-104 in `instance_object_src.go`), only the stored reference marks are restored. Schema marks are missing.\n\n4. **Intermediate Hop 3 - Refresh Execution**: During `terraform refresh` (lines 580-723 in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`), the code:\n   - Extracts marks from the prior state (only reference marks)\n   - Sends unmarked value to provider\n   - Receives unmarked response\n   - Re-applies only the extracted reference marks (line 718-720)\n   - Does NOT apply schema marks (never calls `schema.ValueMarks()`)\n\n5. **Intermediate Hop 4 - Plan Starts**: In the plan phase (lines 725+), the code receives the refreshed state as \"prior state.\" This prior state has only reference marks, NOT schema marks.\n\n6. **Intermediate Hop 5 - Mark Extraction**: Config marks are extracted from configuration (line 868), prior marks are extracted from refreshed state (line 869). These may differ:\n   - Config marks depend on what variables are used (e.g., is `password = var.db_password`?)\n   - Prior marks depend on what was stored in state (only reference marks)\n   - Schema marks are NOT in either set\n\n7. **ROOT CAUSE - Phantom Update Trigger** (line 1208): The plan comparison logic checks if marks are equal. Because schema marks were never applied to the refreshed state, the mark comparison fails even though the values are identical:\n   ```go\n   if action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n       action = plans.Update  // <- WRONG!\n   }\n   ```\n   - `filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths)`: config marks from config\n   - `priorPaths`: reference marks from state (missing schema marks!)\n   - These are different \u2192 action changed to Update\n\n8. **Final Symptom**: Plan shows resource \"will be updated in-place\" even though no actual attribute values changed, only sensitivity mark metadata differs.\n\n## Recommendation\n\nThe fix requires applying schema-derived sensitivity marks at the appropriate point in the refresh\u2192plan flow:\n\n**Option A (Recommended)**: Apply schema marks during refresh after receiving the provider response.\n\nIn `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, modify the `refresh()` method (around lines 717-720) to:\n```go\n// Mark the value if necessary\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}\n\n// ADDITION: Also apply schema-derived marks\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    unmarked, marks := ret.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(unmarked, nil)...)\n    ret.Value = unmarked.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\n```\n\nThis ensures the refreshed state has both reference marks AND schema marks before being passed to the plan phase.\n\n**Option B**: Apply schema marks when extracting prior marks in the plan phase.\n\nIn `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, modify the `plan()` method (around lines 868-869) to ensure schema marks are included when extracting `priorPaths`.\n\n**Option C**: Store schema marks in state files.\n\nModify `instance_object.go` to calculate and store schema-derived marks in `AttrSensitivePaths`, though this requires schema context during state serialization.\n\n**Diagnostic Steps**:\n\n1. Verify that schema marks are missing from refreshed state when compared to the planned value's marks\n3. Confirm that phantom updates disappear once schema marks are applied during refresh\n4. # Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes in Terraform

## Summary

Terraform generates phantom in-place update actions for resources with schema-defined sensitive attributes due to an asymmetry in how sensitivity marks are handled: schema-derived sensitivity marks are applied only during expression evaluation (in `evaluate.go`), not during the refresh-to-plan comparison phase in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`. This causes the mark-based action override at line 1208 to incorrectly convert NoOp to Update when schema-sensitive attributes are present, even though the underlying attribute values are identical.

## Root Cause

The root cause is a critical asymmetry in sensitivity mark propagation across three phases:

1. **Refresh Phase** (`node_resource_abstract_instance.go:718-720`): Marks from prior state are extracted, provider is called with unmarked values, and then only the extracted marks are re-applied. Schema-derived marks are NOT applied.

2. **Plan Comparison Phase** (`node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208`): A mark-equality check compares config marks against refresh marks. Because schema marks were never applied to the refreshed state, the mark sets differ, triggering an erroneous action upgrade from NoOp to Update.

3. **Expression Evaluation Phase** (`evaluate.go:714-723`): Schema-derived marks ARE applied when values are read for expression evaluation, but this happens AFTER planning and is NOT reflected in the plan comparison.

This creates a cascade where:
- State is stored WITHOUT schema marks (line `instance_object.go:131`)
- State is decoded without schema marks (line `instance_object_src.go:90`)
- Refresh doesn't apply schema marks (line `node_resource_abstract_instance.go:718-720`)
- Plan comparis
... (truncated)
